Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

How much crashed? 



<b class="line"><!---->How much crashed? <!----></b>





 Just one tab



<span class="line"><!----> Just one tab<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Is it a problem with a plugin? 



<b class="line"><!---->Is it a problem with a plugin? <!----></b>





 No - It's the browser itself



<span class="line"><!----> No - It's the browser itself<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Steps to reproduce the problem:



<b class="line"><!---->Steps to reproduce the problem:<!----></b>



<br>





1. build chromium with flags "is_asan=true; is_debug=true"



<span class="line"><!---->1. build chromium with flags "is_asan=true; is_debug=true"<!----></span>



<br>





2. setup chromium and open the the HTML file



<span class="line"><!---->2. setup chromium and open the the HTML file<!----></span>



<br>





3. wait for a while (within 10min), and a crash occurs.



<span class="line"><!---->3. wait for a while (within 10min), and a crash occurs.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<b class="line"><!---->Problem Description:<!----></b>

<span class="line"><!---->```Notice that in the HTML file, the front part is pure HTML + CSS downloaded from website.<!----></span>

. Nothing happened after ~20min.



<span class="line"><!---->. Nothing happened after ~20min.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





+ kojii@, the stacktrace seems to point toward a DCHECK. Would you be able to infer what kind of bug this is from the stack trace?



<span class="line"><!---->+ kojii@, the stacktrace seems to point toward a DCHECK. Would you be able to infer what kind of bug this is from the stack trace?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The DCHECK points toward:



<span class="line"><!---->The DCHECK points toward:<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





      DCHECK(single_);  // <--- HERE.



<span class="line"><!---->      DCHECK(single_);  // &lt;--- HERE.<!----></span>



<br>





      return single_->ink_overflow;



<span class="line"><!---->      return single_-&gt;ink_overflow;<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So this is a nullptr dereference. Without the DCHECK, it would crash on the next line.



<span class="line"><!---->So this is a nullptr dereference. Without the DCHECK, it would crash on the next line.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Given 



<span class="line"><!---->Given <!----></span>





https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/HEAD/docs/security/severity-guidelines.md#toc-not-a-security-bug



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/HEAD/docs/security/severity-guidelines.md#toc-not-a-security-bug"><!---->https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/HEAD/docs/security/severity-guidelines.md#toc-not-a-security-bug<!----></a>



<br>





This is not considered a "security" bug, but a real bug anyway.



<span class="line"><!---->This is not considered a "security" bug, but a real bug anyway.<!----></span>
